<p><i><b>Nodame Cantabile</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">のだめカンタービレ</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <i>Nodame Kantābire</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> by <a href="/wiki/Tomoko_Ninomiya" title="Tomoko Ninomiya">Tomoko Ninomiya</a>. It was serialized in Japan by <a href="/wiki/Kodansha" title="Kodansha">Kodansha</a> in the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Kiss_(Japanese_magazine)" title="Kiss (Japanese magazine)">Kiss</a></i> from July 2001 to October 2009 and collected in 23 <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes. A two-volume sequel, called <i>Nodame Cantabile: Opera Chapter</i>, which began serialization in the December 2009 issue of <i>Kiss</i>, was released in 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is licensed in North America by <a href="/wiki/Del_Rey_Manga" title="Del Rey Manga">Del Rey Manga</a>. The series depicts the relationship between two aspiring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_musicians" title="Classical musicians">classical musicians</a>, Megumi "Nodame" Noda and Shinichi Chiaki, as university students and after graduation. It received the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_Manga_Award" title="Kodansha Manga Award">Kodansha Manga Award</a> for best <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Djo_manga" title="Shōjo manga">shōjo manga</a>.</p>
<p>The series has been adapted as four different television series: as an award-winning <a href="/wiki/Japanese_television_drama" title="Japanese television drama">Japanese live-action drama</a> that aired in 2006 followed by a sequel television special that aired in January 2008, as an <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> series spanning three seasons with the first broadcast in 2007, the second in 2008 and the third in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-anime3-announce_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-anime3-announce-2">[2]</a></sup> Two live-action movie sequels to the Japanese television drama, with the same actors, were produced with release dates of 18 December 2009 and April 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-movies-announce_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-movies-announce-3">[3]</a></sup> In addition, several soundtrack albums of classical music have been released, as well as three video games. A <a href="/wiki/Korean_drama" title="Korean drama">South Korean drama</a> live action adaptation aired on the KBS network in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enewsWorld_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-enewsWorld-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dramabeans_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dramabeans-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016 a final installment was published in the April edition of <i>Kiss</i>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nodame_Cantabile_characters" title="List of Nodame Cantabile characters">List of Nodame Cantabile characters</a></div>
<p>Shinichi Chiaki, an <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/arrogant" title="wikt:arrogant">arrogant</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multilingual" title="Multilingual">multilingual</a> perfectionist, is the top student at Momogaoka College of Music and has secret ambitions to become a conductor. Born into a musical family, he is talented in piano and violin and once lived abroad in the music capitals of the world as a young boy (namely Prague), but is trapped in Japan because of his childhood phobia of airplanes and the ocean. In contrast, Megumi Noda, or "Nodame", is a piano student at Momogaoka, notorious for messiness and eccentric behavior. Despite being very talented, Nodame prefers to play by ear rather than according to the musical score; thus, she is regarded as sloppy and playful.</p>
<p>When they meet by accident, Nodame quickly falls in love, but it takes much longer for Chiaki to even begin to appreciate Nodame's unusual qualities. Their relationship causes them both to develop and grow. Along the way, they meet some crazy people (like Masumi, Mine, and Stresemann) and make lasting friendships. Because of Nodame, Chiaki gets the opportunity to lead a student orchestra and begins to have a broader appreciation of people's musical abilities. Because of Chiaki, Nodame faces her fears and enters a piano competition. Opportunities open up as both begin taking risks, stretching themselves far more than they ever thought possible.</p>
<p>After graduation, Nodame succeeds in curing Chiaki from his phobias and they both move to Paris, where Nodame continues her piano studies at the <a href="/wiki/Conservatoire_de_Paris" title="Conservatoire de Paris">Conservatoire de Paris</a> while Chiaki starts a professional career as a conductor. In Europe, they encounter new friends and rivals, as well as keep in touch with their friends from Japan.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tomoko Ninomiya based the character of Megumi Noda on a real-life counterpart with the same name. Ninomiya first learned about the real Noda when the latter, a music college student at the time, posted a photograph of her messy room on a website Ninomiya managed. This inspired her to start a comedy series about a sloppy music student. Ninomiya consults with Noda about musical details, claiming to receive inspiration from her, and thanks Noda in the acknowledgments of every <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volume of <i>Nodame Cantabile</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nodame-real1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-nodame-real1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Noda, currently a piano teacher in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fukuoka,_Fukuoka" title="Fukuoka, Fukuoka">Fukuoka</a> (the home-town of her fictional counterpart), composed the music and co-wrote (with Ninomiya) the lyrics for the "Fart Song" Nodame plays in the first episode of the anime series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nodame-real1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-nodame-real1-6">[6]</a></sup> and visited Ninomiya upon the birth of her son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noda-visit_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-noda-visit-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ninomiya also based the character of James DePreist, the musical director of the fictional Roux-Marlet Orchestra in Paris, on a real-life counterpart with the same name. <a href="/wiki/James_DePreist" title="James DePreist">James DePreist</a> was Permanent Conductor of the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Symphony Orchestra">Tokyo Metropolitan Symphony Orchestra</a>, and conducted the <a class="external text" href="http://www.nodame-orche.com/" rel="nofollow">Nodame Orchestra</a>, which provided the music for both the live-action drama and the anime adaptations.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manga">Manga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Manga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nodame_Cantabile_chapters" title="List of Nodame Cantabile chapters">List of Nodame Cantabile chapters</a></div>
<p>The <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> manga was written and illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Tomoko_Ninomiya" title="Tomoko Ninomiya">Tomoko Ninomiya</a>. It was serialized by <a href="/wiki/Kodansha" title="Kodansha">Kodansha</a> in the biweekly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josei" title="Josei">josei</a> (aimed at younger adult women) manga magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Kiss_(Japanese_magazine)" title="Kiss (Japanese magazine)">Kiss</a></i> from July 10, 2001, to October 10, 2009. The untitled chapters have been collected in 23 <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes. It was licensed in North America by <a href="/wiki/Del_Rey_Manga" title="Del Rey Manga">Del Rey Manga</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delrey1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-delrey1-9">[9]</a></sup> which released 16 of the 23 volumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 2016 <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_USA" title="Kodansha USA">Kodansha USA</a> announced that they received the rights to the series for digital release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It is licensed in France by <a href="/wiki/Pika_%C3%89dition" title="Pika Édition">Pika Édition</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pika_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-pika-12">[12]</a></sup> in South Korea by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daiwon_C.I." title="Daiwon C.I.">Daiwon C.I.</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daiwon-v1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-daiwon-v1-13">[13]</a></sup> in Thailand by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NED_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NED Comics (page does not exist)">NED Comics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NED-v1_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NED-v1-14">[14]</a></sup> in Indonesia by <a href="/wiki/Elex_Media_Komputindo" title="Elex Media Komputindo">Elex Media Komputindo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and in Taiwan by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tong_Li_Comics" title="Tong Li Comics">Tong Li Comics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> All volume covers feature Nodame with a musical instrument.</p>
<p>Starting in May 2008, Japanese serialization changed from biweekly to monthly because of Ninomiya's pregnancy. Serialization went on hiatus starting October 2008 following the birth of her son and Ninomiya's subsequent diagnosis of having <a href="/wiki/Carpal_tunnel_syndrome" title="Carpal tunnel syndrome">carpal tunnel syndrome</a>, but resumed again with the March 10, 2009 issue of <i>Kiss</i> on an irregular schedule depending on her continued recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-hiatus_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-hiatus-17">[17]</a></sup> In June 2009, the series went on hiatus again when Ninomiya was hospitalized with acute appendicitis, and resumed serialization in the July 25 issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-hiatus2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-hiatus2-18">[18]</a></sup> In July 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Asahi_Shimbun" title="Asahi Shimbun">Asahi Shimbun</a></i> reported that the manga was scheduled to end in the spring of 2010, coinciding with the release of the final live-action movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-hiatus2_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-hiatus2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shimbun-end_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-shimbun-end-19">[19]</a></sup> However, the series ended with chapter 136 in the October 10, 2009 issue of the magazine.</p>
<p>Starting in late 2009, a sequel titled <i>Nodame Cantabile - Opera Hen</i> started running in the same magazine. It ended in September 2010. The numbering of the volumes follow right after the original series so they start at volume 24.</p>
<p>On 25 February 2016 in the April 2016 edition of <i>Kiss</i>, Ninomiya published, a one shot set five years after the last installment, it has been described as a final coda to Nodame and Chiaki's story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live-action_drama">Live-action drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Live-action drama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Nodame Cantabile</i> has been adapted as a live-action <a href="/wiki/Japanese_television_drama" title="Japanese television drama">television drama</a> broadcast in 11 hour-long episodes from October 16 to December 25, 2006, on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuji_TV" title="Fuji TV">Fuji TV</a>, covering events up to volume 9 of the manga. This was followed by a four-hour sequel television special, <i>Nodame Cantabile New Year's Special in Europe</i>, adapting further events in the manga after Chiaki and Nodame move to Paris, broadcast on Fuji TV on January 4 and 5, 2008. These were directed by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hideki_Takeuchi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hideki Takeuchi (page does not exist)">Hideki Takeuchi</a> from scripts by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rin_Etou&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rin Etou (page does not exist)">Rin Etou</a>, and starred <a href="/wiki/Hiroshi_Tamaki" title="Hiroshi Tamaki">Hiroshi Tamaki</a> as Shinichi Chiaki and <a href="/wiki/Juri_Ueno" title="Juri Ueno">Juri Ueno</a> as Megumi "Nodame" Noda.</p>
<p>Music direction was by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Daisuke_Mogi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Daisuke Mogi (page does not exist)">Daisuke Mogi</a> with original music by <a href="/wiki/Takayuki_Hattori" title="Takayuki Hattori">Takayuki Hattori</a>, with several works of classical music featured in each episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drama-music-ep1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-drama-music-ep1-21">[21]</a></sup> The orchestral music was performed by Nodame Orchestra, which consisted of members specially selected for the live-action drama with professional support from the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Symphony Orchestra">Tokyo Metropolitan Symphony Orchestra</a>. The Orchestra was conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_DePriest" title="James DePriest">James DePriest</a>, Permanent Conductor of the Tokyo Metropolitan Orchestra, who would later have his name and likeness used in the Nodame storyline as the musical director of the fictional Roux-Marlet Orchestra. The opening theme for both the drama series and special was the First movement ("Andante Cantabile") from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beethoven" title="Beethoven">Beethoven</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._7_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 7 (Beethoven)">Symphony No. 7</a></i>, and the ending theme was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gershwin" title="Gershwin">Gershwin</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rhapsody_in_Blue" title="Rhapsody in Blue">Rhapsody in Blue</a></i>, both performed by the Nodame Orchestra conducted by Toshiaki Umeda.</p>
<p>An episode of <i>PuriGorota: Uchū no Yūjō Daibōken</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">プリごろ太 宇宙の友情大冒険</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, the fictional anime series that Nodame watches, was created by <a href="/wiki/J.C.Staff" title="J.C.Staff">J.C.Staff</a> for the drama. The anime was written and directed by <a href="/wiki/Ken%27ichi_Kasai" title="Ken'ichi Kasai">Ken'ichi Kasai</a>, the director of the first season of the <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> <a href="/wiki/Nodame_Cantabile#Anime" title="Nodame Cantabile">anime</a>. Segments of the <i>PuriGorota</i> anime were shown during episode 4 of the <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> drama, with the complete anime released as a DVD extra with the <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> anime series.</p>
<p>Two live-action movie sequels to the television drama with the same actors were produced, with the first film being released in December 2009, while the second film was released in April 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-movies-announce_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-movies-announce-3">[3]</a></sup> Filming began in May 2009 and lasted for five months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and included location filming in Vienna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-hiatus2_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-ann-hiatus2-18">[18]</a></sup> On May 4, 2009, the drama began airing in the Philippines on the <a href="/wiki/GMA_Network" title="GMA Network">GMA Network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In South Korea the drama aired on <a href="/wiki/Munhwa_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Munhwa Broadcasting Corporation">MBC</a>'s cable channel where it achieved peak ratings of 2%, which is a record high for a foreign cable drama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Korean_drama" title="Korean drama">South Korean</a> adaptation titled <i><a href="/wiki/Cantabile_Tomorrow" title="Cantabile Tomorrow">Cantabile Tomorrow</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Joo_Won" title="Joo Won">Joo Won</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shim_Eun-kyung" title="Shim Eun-kyung">Shim Eun-kyung</a> aired on <a href="/wiki/KBS2" title="KBS2">KBS2</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enewsWorld_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-enewsWorld-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dramabeans_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dramabeans-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">Anime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Anime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nodame_Cantabile_episodes" title="List of Nodame Cantabile episodes">List of Nodame Cantabile episodes</a></div>
<p><i>Nodame Cantabile</i> was also adapted as an <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> television series, produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuji_TV" title="Fuji TV">Fuji TV</a> and animated by <a href="/wiki/J.C.Staff" title="J.C.Staff">J.C.Staff</a>. The series was broadcast on Fuji and associated stations in the <a href="/wiki/Noitamina" title="Noitamina">Noitamina</a> time slot. The first season, titled <i>Nodame Cantabile</i>, was broadcast in 23 episodes from January 11 to June 28, 2007, and the second season, called <i>Nodame Cantabile: Paris Chapter</i>, was broadcast in 11 episodes from October 8 to December 18, 2008. Both seasons were also later aired in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite television</a> network <a href="/wiki/Animax" title="Animax">Animax</a>. The first season was directed by <a href="/wiki/Ken%27ichi_Kasai" title="Ken'ichi Kasai">Ken'ichi Kasai</a> (the director of the <i><a href="/wiki/Honey_and_Clover" title="Honey and Clover">Honey and Clover</a></i> anime) and the second season by <a href="/wiki/Chiaki_Kon" title="Chiaki Kon">Chiaki Kon</a>, and starred <a href="/wiki/Ayako_Kawasumi" title="Ayako Kawasumi">Ayako Kawasumi</a> as Megumi "Nodame" Noda and <a href="/wiki/Tomokazu_Seki" title="Tomokazu Seki">Tomokazu Seki</a> as Shinichi Chiaki. An <a href="/wiki/Original_video_animation" title="Original video animation">original video animation</a> (OVA) episode was included with the limited edition volume 22 of the manga when it was published in Japan on 10 August 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann21_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann21-25">[25]</a></sup> and a third and final anime season, called <i>Nodame Cantabile: Finale</i> began airing in January 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-anime3-announce_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-anime3-announce-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-hiatus2_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-ann-hiatus2-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 6, 2009, the series received its <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> television premiere on <a href="/wiki/Animax_Asia" title="Animax Asia">Animax Asia</a> across its networks in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, airing the series with its original Japanese audio and English subtitles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and later its air in English Dubbed on 12 June 2009.</p>
<p>The music director for both seasons was <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Suguru_Matsutani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Suguru Matsutani (page does not exist)">Suguru Matsutani</a>. As with the live-action drama, several works of classical music were featured in each episode,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animeplanet-music_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-animeplanet-music-27">[27]</a></sup> performed by the Nodame Orchestra. The opening theme of season one was "Allegro Cantabile" by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suemitsu_%26_The_Suemith" title="Suemitsu &amp; The Suemith">Suemitsu &amp; The Suemith</a>, and the ending themes were "<a href="/wiki/Konna_ni_Chikaku_de..." title="Konna ni Chikaku de...">Konna ni Chikaku de...</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Kay" title="Crystal Kay">Crystal Kay</a> (episodes 1–12), "Sagittarius" by Suemitsu &amp; the Nodame Orchestra (episodes 13–22), and "Allegro Cantabile" by Suemitsu &amp; The Suemith (episode 23). The opening theme for the second season was "Sky High" by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Gospellers" title="The Gospellers">The Gospellers</a> (with melody taken from the Third movement ("Allegro Scherzando") of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rachmaninoff" title="Rachmaninoff">Rachmaninoff</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._2_(Rachmaninoff)" title="Piano Concerto No. 2 (Rachmaninoff)">Piano Concerto No. 2</a>), and the ending theme was "Tokyo et Paris" <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">東京 et Paris</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>, lit. "Tokyo and Paris")</span> by <a href="/wiki/Emiri_Miyamoto" title="Emiri Miyamoto">Emiri Miyamoto</a> x solita (with variations on the theme from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravel" title="Ravel">Ravel</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%A9ro" title="Boléro">Boléro</a></i>). The opening theme for the final season is "Manazashi Daydream" by Yuu Sakai (with variations on the theme from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bach" title="Bach">Bach</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Jesu,_Joy_of_Man%27s_Desiring" title="Jesu, Joy of Man's Desiring">Jesu, Joy of Man's Desiring</a></i>) and the ending theme is "Kaze to Oka no Ballad (風と丘のバラード)" by Real Paradis with Nodame Orchestra.</p>
<p>The first season was released on 8 DVDs between April and November 2007. A box set was released in February 2008 with an additional 15-minute <a href="/wiki/Original_video_animation" title="Original video animation">original video animation</a> (OVA), taking place between episodes 8 and 9. The series has been licensed in Russia<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and South Korea. The first DVD of the second season was released on 24 December 2008.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(January 2009)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Several albums of classical music have been released in association with <i>Nodame Cantabile</i>. Some were promotional tie-ins with the manga, while others are soundtrack albums for the live-action and anime series.</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile</i> - Released in September 2003 (ISBN B0000C4GLG), with sections of music by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rachmaninov" title="Rachmaninov">Rachmaninov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liszt" title="Liszt">Liszt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahms" title="Brahms">Brahms</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gershwin" title="Gershwin">Gershwin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beethoven" title="Beethoven">Beethoven</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chopin" title="Chopin">Chopin</a> that are performed by the characters in the manga series. The performers included the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Philharmonic" title="Vienna Philharmonic">Vienna Philharmonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Philharmonic" title="Berlin Philharmonic">Berlin Philharmonic</a>.</li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile Selection CD Book</i> - Published on August 10, 2005, by Kodansha (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9784063646467">ISBN 978-4-06-364646-7</a>) as a book with accompanying CD. The CD includes works by Beethoven, Rachmaninov, Gershwin, Liszt, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozart" title="Mozart">Mozart</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Debussy" title="Debussy">Debussy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravel" title="Ravel">Ravel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a> that are performed by characters in the manga series. The book includes commentaries by music critic Sakuma.</li>
<li><i>Brahms Symphony Number 1: Nodame Cantabile</i> - Released in September 2005 by <a href="/wiki/King_Records_(Japan)" title="King Records (Japan)">King Records</a> (ISBN B000ALJ16S), with recordings of Brahms's <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._1_(Brahms)" title="Symphony No. 1 (Brahms)"><i>Symphony No. 1</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Franz_Schubert" title="Franz Schubert">Schubert</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._8_(Schubert)" title="Symphony No. 8 (Schubert)"><i>Symphony No. 8 "Unfinished"</i></a>, which are performed in the series by the R☆S Orchestra. 50,000 copies had been sold by the end of October 2005, the month after release.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile Selection CD Book vol.2</i> - Published in August 2006 by Kodansha (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9784063646665">ISBN 978-4-06-364666-5</a>), covering music that appeared in the manga series since the release of the first <i>Selection CD Book</i>, including pieces by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berlioz" title="Berlioz">Berlioz</a>, Ravel, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stravinsky" title="Stravinsky">Stravinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Franck" title="César Franck">Franck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dukas" title="Paul Dukas">Dukas</a>, and Mozart. Included in the book are commentaries by oboist and conductor Daisuke Mogi and music professor Osawa Tetsu.</li>
<li><i>Nodame Orchestra LIVE!</i> - Released on November 15, 2006 (ISBN B000I5YAD0) as a 2-CD soundtrack for the live-action drama as performed by the Nodame Orchestra. It included works by Beethoven, Gershwin, Mozart, Brahms, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_de_Sarasate" title="Pablo de Sarasate">Pablo de Sarasate</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bach" title="Bach">Bach</a>, Chopin, Debussy, Stravinsky, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schubert" title="Schubert">Schubert</a>. This reached number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> album chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-album-record_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-album-record-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Nodame Orchestra STORY!</i> - Released on February 21, 2007 (ISBN B000M7XSPU) as a 2-CD soundtrack from the first season of the anime series, again performed by the Nodame Orchestra. It included works as supposedly performed by the fictional student ensembles S Orchestra, A Orchestra, and R☆S Orchestra. It included works by Beethoven, Mozart, Chopin, Bartók, Dvořák, Gershwin, Rachmaninov, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Jolivet" title="André Jolivet">André Jolivet</a>, Listz, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-Sa%C3%ABns" title="Saint-Saëns">Saint-Saëns</a>, Elgar, Bach, Brahms, Schubert, Debussy, Schumann, Stravinsky, and de Sarasate.</li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile Selection CD Book vol.3</i> - Released in August 2008 (<a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9784063646665">ISBN 978-4-06-364666-5</a>), covering music that appeared in volumes 16–20 of manga series, since the release of the second <i>Selection CD Book</i>. It included works by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rossini" title="Rossini">Rossini</a>, Chopin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tchaikovsky" title="Tchaikovsky">Tchaikovsky</a>, Bach, and Debussy.</li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile: Paris Chapter</i> - Released on October 15, 2008 (ISBN B001DNF70Q) as a 2-CD soundtrack from the second season of anime series, again performed by the Nodame Orchestra.</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, <i>Nodame Cantabile Special BEST!</i> Released in December 2007, a "best-of" compilation of the most popular works from these albums to date.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Games">Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Three <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> games have been released in Japan:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile</i> for <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a>, released on April 19, 2007, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namco_Bandai_Games" title="Namco Bandai Games">Namco Bandai Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-game-ds-ign_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-game-ds-ign-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bandai-ds_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-bandai-ds-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile</i> for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a>, released on July 19, 2007, by <a href="/wiki/Banpresto" title="Banpresto">Banpresto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-banpresto-ps2_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-banpresto-ps2-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Nodame Cantabile: Dream Orchestra</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">のだめカンタービレ ドリーム☆オーケストラ</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> for <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> console, released on December 27, 2007, by Namco Bandai Games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bandai-wii_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bandai-wii-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The manga of <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> received the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_Manga_Award" title="Kodansha Manga Award">Kodansha Manga Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Djo" title="Shōjo">shōjo</a> manga,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KodanshaHahn_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-KodanshaHahn-33">[33]</a></sup> and was a jury recommendation at both the 2005 and 2008 <a href="/wiki/Japan_Media_Arts_Festival" title="Japan Media Arts Festival">Japan Media Arts Festivals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmaf2005_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-jmaf2005-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmaf2008_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-jmaf2008-35">[35]</a></sup> It was a finalist for the <a href="/wiki/Tezuka_Osamu_Cultural_Prize" title="Tezuka Osamu Cultural Prize">Tezuka Osamu Cultural Prize</a> in 2005 and 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tezuka2005_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-tezuka2005-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tezuka2006_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-tezuka2006-37">[37]</a></sup> but did not win. In 2006, the English translation was named by the New York Public Library as one of the Books for the Teen Age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The series sold 2.8 million copies in 2008, making it the 8th best-selling manga series in Japan that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Volume 17 was the third best-selling manga on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> charts for 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestselling-17_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-bestselling-17-40">[40]</a></sup> and volumes 20 and 21 were the 6th and 7th best-selling manga on the Oricon charts for 2008, respectively, selling 1.2 million copies each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestselling-20-21_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-bestselling-20-21-41">[41]</a></sup> According to an Oricon survey men and women aged 10–40, <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> was the second "most interesting" manga series published during 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top-manga-2008_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-top-manga-2008-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The series and its associated music albums are credited with increasing sales of classical music in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> As a whole, the series is a best-seller in Japan, having sold over 37 million copies as of March 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The English translation of <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> has been praised for its quirky, interesting characters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v11_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v11-46">[46]</a></sup> sense of humor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v15_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v15-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-libjournal-v2_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-libjournal-v2-48">[48]</a></sup> and clean art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v5-6_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v5-6-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mania-v1-art_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-mania-v1-art-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Deppey" title="Dirk Deppey">Dirk Deppey</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Comics_Journal" title="The Comics Journal">The Comics Journal</a></i> praised Ninomiya's storytelling, saying she "has a solid sense of when to accentuate the highs and lows with just the right note, and understands that one can only do this by not hitting such notes very often", resulting in "an understated soap opera" that is "a seamless and enjoyable storytelling experience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deppley-v6_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-deppley-v6-51">[51]</a></sup> Reviewers have called Ninomiya's character development subtle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v5-6_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v5-6-49">[49]</a></sup> while noting it is the character interactions that drive the story,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v14-c_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v14-c-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mania-v13_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-mania-v13-53">[53]</a></sup> and that "each character has a real and lasting effect on others."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v5-6_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v5-6-49">[49]</a></sup> Reviewers also cite Ninomiya's ability to depict "scenes of people playing music that no one can hear" and her sense of humor as factors in the series' appeal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v11_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v11-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v15_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v15-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v10_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v10-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v14-a_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v14-a-55">[55]</a></sup> Ninomiya has been criticized for not handling transitions between storylines well,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v11b_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v11b-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mania-v10-transition_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-mania-v10-transition-57">[57]</a></sup> for sometimes letting the characters derail the story,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v14-a_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v14-a-55">[55]</a></sup> and for art and backgrounds that are sometimes too plain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v5-6_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v5-6-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-v14-b_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-v14-b-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mania-v1-backgrounds_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-mania-v1-backgrounds-59">[59]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Thorn" title="Matt Thorn">Matt Thorn</a> criticized the English translation for inaccuracies of tone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thorn-trans_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-thorn-trans-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The live-action drama received the 2007 Japanese Drama Academy Awards for Best Drama, Best Lead Actress (<a href="/wiki/Juri_Ueno" title="Juri Ueno">Juri Ueno</a>), Best Direction (Hideki Takeuchi), Best Music (<a href="/wiki/Takayuki_Hattori" title="Takayuki Hattori">Takayuki Hattori</a>), and Best Title Song;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jdrama-awards_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-jdrama-awards-61">[61]</a></sup> the show was also recognized overseas as Best Miniseries at the 2nd Seoul Drama Festival.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Juri Ueno also was named Best Newcomer at the Élan d'or Awards for her performance,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and the next year was named Best Actress at the International Drama Festival in Tokyo Awards for reprising her role as Nodame in the television special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tdrama-awards_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-tdrama-awards-62">[62]</a></sup> The <i>New Year's Special in Europe</i> received an average household rating of 20.3% and 21.0% for the two nights it was broadcast in Japan, making it them the highest-rated drama episodes of the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-tvspec-rating_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-tvspec-rating-63">[63]</a></sup> The first soundtrack album for the drama, <i>Nodame Orchestra LIVE!</i>, reached number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> album chart, breaking the record for highest ranked classical music album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-album-record_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-album-record-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The opening episode of the anime series broke the record for audience share for its time-slot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record-rating_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-record-rating-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The first DVD volume debuted at number 3 on the Oricon chart for anime the week it went on sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DVD1-sales_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-DVD1-sales-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the anime has not been licensed in English, it has still received notice from English reviewers, who praised the character development and chemistry, the balance between drama and comedy, voice acting, and especially the music—both the performances and how it was presented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animeplanet-s1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-animeplanet-s1-67">[67]</a></sup> Reviewers did complain that the visual design of some secondary characters were too similar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animeplanet-s1_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-animeplanet-s1-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, a cafe based on <i>Nodame Cantabile</i> opened in <a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a>, Tokyo, including live music from the live-action drama and sets from the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann-cafe_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann-cafe-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nodame_Cantabile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-mania-v1-art-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mania-v1-art_50-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Chavez, Eduardo M. <li id="cite_note-mania-v13-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mania-v13_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Van Gorder, Danielle (2 September 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://www.mania.com/nodame-cantabile-vol-13_article_81716.html" rel="nofollow">"Nodame Cantabile Vol. #13"</a>. Mania.com<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>This series is all about the characters and the changing dynamics between them, and the various members of the supporting cast really do a lot to drive the series along.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Danielle&amp;rft.aulast=Van+Gorder&amp;rft.btitle=Nodame+Cantabile+Vol.+%2313&amp;rft.date=2008-09-02&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mania.com%2Fnodame-cantabile-vol-13_article_81716.html&amp;rft.pub=Mania.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-ann-v10-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ann-v10_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Santos, Carlo (5 September 2007). <a class="external text" href="http://www.animenewsnetwork.com/review/nodame-cantabile/gn-10" rel="nofollow">"Review: Nodame Cantabile: GN 10"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>The series' artwork is at its most expressive when it comes to the music performance scenes ... sweeping lines, impressionistic backgrounds, and closeups that almost make it feel like being there... Ninomiya also uses layouts to her advantage—notice, for example, how the panels become more angular and compressed when Chiaki stresses out on his final assignment.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Carlo&amp;rft.aulast=Santos&amp;rft.btitle=Review%3A+Nodame+Cantabile%3A+GN+10&amp;rft.date=2007-09-05&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.animenewsnetwork.com%2Freview%2Fnodame-cantabile%2Fgn-10&amp;rft.pub=Anime+News+Network&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-ann-v14-a-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ann-v14-a_55-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ann-v14-a_55-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Santos, Carlo (19 September 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://www.animenewsnetwork.com/review/nodame-cantabile/gn-14" rel="nofollow">"Review: Nodame Cantabile: GN 14"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>If there is any criticism to be had, it's that Tomoko Ninomiya seems to be having so much fun portraying the characters that the storyline sometimes gets off track.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Carlo&amp;rft.aulast=Santos&amp;rft.btitle=Review%3A+Nodame+Cantabile%3A+GN+14&amp;rft.date=2008-09-19&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.animenewsnetwork.com%2Freview%2Fnodame-cantabile%2Fgn-14&amp;rft.pub=Anime+News+Network&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-ann-v11b-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ann-v11b_56-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Santos, Carlo (30 November 2007). <a class="external text" href="http://www.animenewsnetwork.com/review/nodame-cantabile/gn-11" rel="nofollow">"Review: Nodame Cantabile: GN 11"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>The transition to the next stage of the story, however, is not quite as graceful: it takes some really stupid, improbable plot twists to get Chiaki into Stresemann's world tour, and their itinerary turns out to be even more outlandish.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Carlo&amp;rft.aulast=Santos&amp;rft.btitle=Review%3A+Nodame+Cantabile%3A+GN+11&amp;rft.date=2007-11-30&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.animenewsnetwork.com%2Freview%2Fnodame-cantabile%2Fgn-11&amp;rft.pub=Anime+News+Network&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-mania-v10-transition-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mania-v10-transition_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Chavez, Eduardo M. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>After so much build up leading to Noda and Chiaki's decision to take their talents abroad, little of the preparation was discussed. Instead, Ninomiya fresh from a trip to France, jumped right into this next chapter</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Eduardo+M.&amp;rft.aulast=Chavez&amp;rft.btitle=Nodame+Cantabile+Vol.+%2310&amp;rft.date=2007-10-10&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mania.com%2Fnodame-cantabile-vol-10_article_83155.html&amp;rft.pub=Mania.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-ann-v14-b-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ann-v14-b_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Santos, Carlo (19 September 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://www.animenewsnetwork.com/review/nodame-cantabile/gn-14" rel="nofollow">"Review: Nodame Cantabile: GN 14"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 December</span> 2008</span>. <q>Simple but striking character designs also add to the series' unique style, but the one major flaw is in the backgrounds—characters often find themselves standing in front of plain white space, a generic screentone, or a hastily drawn interior</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANodame+Cantabile&amp;rft.aufirst=Carlo&amp;rft.aulast=Santos&amp;rft.btitle=Review%3A+Nodame+Cantabile%3A+GN+14&amp;rft.date=2008-09-19&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.animenewsnetwork.com%2Freview%2Fnodame-cantabile%2Fgn-14&amp;rft.pub=Anime+News+Network&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-mania-v1-backgrounds-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mania-v1-backgrounds_59-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Chavez, Eduardo M.
